RATING: 9.5
An interesting "dungeon-crawl/Ameritrash/dicefest/special abilities" game. Having played several times now, I recall the very first game where the humans (me) got their BUTTS KICKED in SPADES. At first, it was an easy go of it... the trogs were dying very easily. Then they managed to fight back. Misery ensued. All of the other games have been nail-biters or close to being so. Certainly some excitement.

It's certainly not a bad game... It's certainly better than Drakon -- a game this title reminds me of a great deal.

It will get back to the table, as it's an attractive game (heavy cardstock) and has an innovative combat/health mechanic that I think will see more action around here.

This title has superb production value for the price, is basically Space Hulk combined with a little Descent, but with a lot less setup time, a lot more to do, and great replay-ability. Each game is markedly different and exciting. Asmodee has really hit a home-run with this one.

RATING: 10
This game really scratches my itch for a tactical combat minis game.  I ended up with this instead of Space Hulk, due to the price, and I'm very happy with it.

After many plays as both humans and demons, I'm moving my rating from 9 to 10.  I always want to play Claustrophobia.  It's always tense and engaging, with interesting decisions to be had on both sides.

Some people report that this game is unbalanced, but I can win perfectly well with both sides.  I think that the game -feels- unbalanced when you don't understand the strengths and weaknesses of your side, and don't play it properly.

This is my first 10 rating ever, and this game deserves it.

RATING: 7
This is a nicely done two-player dungeon crawler where the priests are against the satanic demons. It is scenario based, and unfortunatelly there are only a few of them but nevertheless each of them has a fair amount of replayability. It has a uniques mechanism where you each turn select the stats of your heroes based on the die you roll. The strategy for the demons is largely based on the fact that they can overwhelm you, the priests must evade. All-in-all it is an easy and relatively quick to learn game. The painted miniatures are awesome.

RATING: 10
Why I think you should play this game: 

*The tactile experience-the aesthetic, the size, the development of the dungeon-is grand without being baroque. This is truly a visual feast. 

*The theme is darker and funnier than your usual Ameritrash traditions: the French production does absurdity and foreboding at the same time.

*The dynamics are very tense-the humans are replete with power but losing strength every turn; the Demon begins weak but grows more and more threatening. It feels cramped and desperate.

*The combat and movement metrics are elegant. Abilites and numbers are straightforward in application but offer varied application when infused with spatial and tempo concerns. 

*Scenarios play in one hour or less. People have complained one side is better than the other too often. Beyond Who Dares Wins (Scenario 6) I don't think this is true to any imbalanced extent. Each side has its strategic biases and situations it doesn't want to be in. Learn them and mitigate them. 

*The online content and the expansion vault this game into the stratosphere for me. I'd play with De Profundis every time once my opponent knew what was going on; it gives the Demon just enough more to do and makes the Humans more nuanced, too.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I am partial to the occasional dungeon crawl, but I like them short and snappy, otherwise I start to wonder why I'm not role-playing instead.  Claustrophobia is certainly quite short; you are plunged straight into fast and furious action and the scenarios are designed to reach a climax quickly.  

I am not so keen on the kind of dungeon crawl that is purely about tactical combat.  Claustrophobia is just that; yet I appreciate its very streamlined approach that eliminates all fiddliness and yet doesn't boil down to a mindless dice fest. On the contrary, Claustrophobia gives you plenty to think about. 

So, I have quite enjoyed my plays so far.  There are a couple of niggles.  First, the scenarios I have tried all  seem to favour the demons. Second, there is little variation in the dramatis personae; there are but three human characters and the troglodytes are always the same old hoard. 

Production quality is stunningly good, with painted minis and big, thick tiles.  I found the artwork a slightly mixed bag, the tiles are beautiful, but I found the card and box artwork rather uninspired.  The rules are reasonably good, though I'd still recommend downloading Universal Head's excellent condensed version.

RATING: 6
I'm not a dungeon crawl fan, but I did enjoy this one. Probably because it is two-players only, so it doesn't fall into the trap other of its kind fall into. The dice-allocation/action selection mechanism seems interesting and provides a nice balance of strategy and luck.

The biggest problem is there is just not enough variety, an absolute requirement for game of this type. The models are nice but are too few and the hero characters are often hard to tell apart from one another. Even if I were a dungeon-crawler, I still wouldn't buy it.

RATING: 7.5
Labirintusban barangolni, szörnyekkel vagdalkozni, harci érték, sebzés - számomra idegen közeg.
... és mégis kellemes időtöltésként értékeltem a vele való "foglalatoskodást".
A játék minősége - magért beszél. (festett figurák, szépen megrajzolt lapkák, stb.)
Játékidő - abszolút optimális.
Újrajátszhatóság - kizárt két azonos - még csak hasonló - parti is.
Szabályrendszer - könnyen előadható és értelmezhető.

RATING: 9
A thematic dungeon crawler with fast paced action and some beautiful painted miniatures. Some tactics and strategy are needed even though game is driven by the dice rolls. Human player is underdog here - he may win from time to time, but even best strategy could be killed by bad rolls. This game is heavy scenario-dependent, so keep in mind there are scenarios easier for one side or another. Still, the first scenario is probably the best one; it gives you full freedom in exploration and is essential to the core of the game mechanisms. Claustrophobia is for people who like thematic games, dungeon crawlers and asymmetric gameplay. And for those who can accept some randomness and unpredictability in exchange for pure fun of exploring and killing. Too bad that while playing as humans is full of tension (they are outnumbered and quickly become weaker as game progresses), playing as demons resembles walk in the park rather (unlike human player, demon player grows stronger and his main forces are usually unlimited). But again, it is thematic-wise. Feel the cold of dark tunnels, smell the stench of abominous foe. Then play this unique game :) 
Highly recommended.

RATING: 8
Initial Impressions: This is a tactical game where substance clearly takes a back seat to style. And that's not a bad thing. The card and tile artwork and prepainted minis carry the theme well and the rules are kept simple in order to not detract from the immersion. The missions promise to introduce additional innovative mechanisms that can be discarded after the adventure is done. Simple rules and mechanisms, however, don't mean that the overall game is light. The main decisions in this game are not where to move and who to target, as is in most tactical games. Instead, the toughest decisions are where to allocate your dice and which order to activate your warriors. I admit that this game surprised me with more tension and decisions than I was expecting and I'll gladly play it some more to see if the rest of the missions are as innovative as the one that I played.

RATING: 9.4
This game really hit me like a hammer. When we first played it, me and my son both shouted AGAIN! This is a great tactical one on one dungeon crawler game. The reason it's so enjoyable is that it's light enough to learn it in 15 minutes, quick enough to play it within an hour, but still deep enough to offer a real challenge. The clever exploring mechanics make even playing the same scenario a different experience everytime. The use of dice to decide what you can do with your characters is different for both sides but still seems very balanced. The way they ensured replayability with limited components is also worth a big compliment. In the end it comes down to the fact that this game is just very much fun to play. Lastly the components are great. Nice thick tiles and cards. The painted miniatures are also well above par.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Claustrophobia is a scenario based dungeon crawl type of game with asymmetrical player powers, simple rules and entertaining gameplay. 

The excellent production values include thick tiles with very good artwork and painted minis which serve to set the mood and transport you to the scene. The minis are pre-painted and although they are not the best paint jobs, it's pleasing to see that they included them.

The gameplay is thematic, engaging, enjoyable and there is room for tactical and strategical choices. The various scenarios seem to be balanced and there are a plethora of them in the game's website. Here is the link for the scenarios:

http://www.claustrophobia-theboardgame.com/en/?cat=8

Although these type of games are not usually my cup of tea, I found this game to be entertaining with tough choices all in under an hour. Yes, there is randomness and a theme that might put you off, but taken for what it is, it is a fun romp.

Have professionally printed and bound scenario and campaign books.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
I am not entirely sure what slowly drove away my enjoyment of this game.  I feel that I should like it, it has a lot of clever new ideas (the use of dice mostly) and I really want a good dungeon crawly game.  Despite this I just find myself bored by the game.  I think that it may just be that the scenarios don't really do a good job of mixing up the play.  Most of the time the humans are just trying to escape which is fun a few times but the stalling tactics become pretty obvious after that.

Another flaw is just how much random events decide your fate.  The demons choices are far too constrained by the dice and the cards vary wildly in power.  By far the worst offender is the board layout and in fact in most scenarios this usually decides the game for us.  A devastating dead end or a convenient choke point often spells the end for the humans.

Lastly, I can't help but feel that demons are less enjoyable.  You are mostly sending weak troggs that get slaughtered the next round to slowly chip away at health.  There are a few tricks, but the way movement works doesn't give you a whole lot of interesting decisions.  Contrast this with the humans who get special cards, items and different redeemer powers each scenario.  Furthermore there dice rolls aren't as constricting and instead allow them to specialize their characters each round.  Finally movement is a lot more tactical with the bodyguard's abilities or Elusive Blades'.  Needless to say, I find the game a lot more enjoyable as the humans.

So in conclusion, I am not sure this really dethrones Doom as my adversarial dungeon crawl game.  The amount of randomness and the disparity between the two sides leads to an unsatisfying game (for at least one person).

RATING: 8
I am very impressed with how many "problems" this game solves. It's strategic and tactical but with an easy rules set. It involves some of the thoughtful choices of Euro games in the context of a fantasy theme. It's a two player competitive dungeon crawl that plays in less than an hour (really). Finally, it is tight and well balanced despite all the choices available to both players. It has beautifully produced components for a reasonable price. There isn't a tremendous amount of variety in the components and substance of the game but this is more than made up for in the simplicity of the ruleset and chits involved. Pound for pound, it's the best dungeon crawl game I've played because its elegance just sets it in another gameplay league than Ravenloft, Descent and company.

RATING: 6
A couple of things on this title.  I want to love it, I really do.  It's great looking, and the components are top notch.  I don't believe that I've seen a set of prepainted minis up to these standards before.  The artwork on the tiles is fantastic!  The art on the cards is ok, the manual is full color and nicely illustrated.  The method of tracking wounds on the humans and this simulating the effects of the wounds is great.

My issues are with the gameplay itself.  The game seems quite random and too light.  We don't feel that we have much control over the humans, while the demon player excersises almost complete control over his forces.  Since everything is totally dice-driven, it's quite difficult to plan ahead with any reasonable amount of certainty, and this adds to the overall feeling of randomness.  While playing this I can't help but feel like I'd much rather be playing Descent for a satisfying dungeon crawling experience, or something else if I did not have that kind of time.

RATING: 8
Hmm, early days so I need to play it a bit more to get a final rating. Was expecting to love it, but was a bit disappointed. It's too tactical for me, in that there is little planning you can really do from turn to turn, rather maximise what you can do NOW. It's too random - but also quite fiddly and complicated. Random tiles, random movement (you might be moving 0,1, or 2 depending ...) random combat ... 

Plus side over space hulk and DOOM is the fast setup - but I prefer the scifi theme. The random setup theoretically is more replayable as you can 'solve' the space hulk scenarios with repeat playings.

Overall felt I'd rather play Lost Patrol for a quick random tactical survival game. For a longer game - Space Hulk wins hands down.

*** Update, more plays and I'm liking this more - the pin rule makes the game really, but is rather dependant on the tiles drawn. It fills a niche, I still prefer space hulk, but the random tiles mean you can't 'solve' each scenario.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
-traded away in a MathTrade-

sleeved

A 2 player dungeon crawler? Is there any possibility that this works well?

Yes and it is called Claustrophobia.

It has a pretty simple and elegant but still really rich system. One player plays a dungeon crawler the other one plays Kingsburg. Yes, Kingsburg, yes, I'm serious.

While the one is exploring the caverns under New-Jerusalem the other one is collection points to summon the demons trying to devour the poor lunatics that try to clear the caverns.

The components are really good. Thick sturdy cardboard, the player tableaus are well made (Formula D-style), good cardstock and the shiny highlight: prepainted miniatures.
I also have to mention the dice. Normally I don't care about my dice but the ones in this game are, I would say, more rounded than normal ones. They feel pretty nice.

The only negative are the two special monster token. They are to small (compared to the mini) to use them on the board, but still too big to put them on the base under the mini.

For everyone who thinks that the scenarios in the rulebook aren't enough there are some on the Asmodee-Homepage.

Sadly this great game doesn't get reprinted.

RATING: 7
Nice! This fills a good niche for when you've only got two players and can't be bothered to setup Descent and devote 2-3 hours to a game.

The dice system both for the humans and demons is pretty nifty and makes the game really feel different for each side. The humans especially have a cool choice point - I love that when you take damage, you have to decide how you want to limit your future stat options.

It might be a weird complaint, but did the tiles have to be SO big? They could easily fit the max number of characters per tile and been a lot smaller... just seems like a lot of wasted space for those of us without huge tables.

It's not the kind of game you can sit down and play several games of in a night, though. I always have fun when I play... it's just... a little bit too shallow for that.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
As you can probably tell by my ~700 ratings, I’m a hardcore Eurogamer. However, this doesn’t mean that I cannot appreciate and even enjoy other types of games. I generally don’t like many Ameritrash games, but Claustrophobia is actually quite a good game!

First of all, Claustrophobia is an Ameritrash game, yes. You’re trying to kill each other (one player is playing as the heroes and the other players is controlling the evil forces), and it has tons of dice rolling which means that the luck factor is quite big (add to this the random tile and card draws). Still, I find it enjoyable. I think the major reason is that I don’t own any other games like this, and I really like the fact that there are several scenarios to play. The random tile draws ensure that the dungeon is going to be different each time, and sometime you get screwed by bad tiles and other times it’s a little too easy. The listed play time of just 45 minutes is pretty spot on, I think all of my games have lasted between a half and one hour, and when you consider this, Claustrophobia is a great game! It’s so easy and fast to play!

I haven’t tried all of the scenarios, but those I have have been very enjoyable and a little different from another (as they should be). Now, you can play as the good guys or the bad guys, but because I’m winning regularly in most of my games, I almost always play the heroes as they have a harder time winning in Claustrophobia. This has resulted in a lot of defeats and only one win and a couple of ties, but I don’t mind. I would like to play the bad guys a little more, though, because they are by far the most interesting side – the dice mechanism (deciding where to put your dice on your board) is just plain awesome!

Having played Claustrophobia 9 times now, which is a lot for me, I’m not sure if I’m going to keep it. The reason for this is not because it’s a bad game, because it isn’t (just look at my rating, which is very high for a game like this!), but because I seldom play 2 player games, and when I do, I often play TS, 1960, Agricola ACBAS, Summoner Wars, Mage Wars and a bunch of other 2 player games – or even some good multiplayer eurogames which support 2 players well like Caylus, Le Havre etc. But Claustrophobia is certainly a good game which is very easy to learn and play!

RATING: 8
Rated 8 after two back-to-back plays of the first scenario. I'm not normally a dungeon crawler type of player, but I was very excited about this game based on reviews and the promise that it offered a thoughtful but light assymmetrical game.

For the first two plays, this game really delivered. Turns are quick, but there's fun choices to make. Each side feels very different. It's surprisingly thematic, and at least the first scenario creates a good sense of drama and tension. If want to own a dungeon crawl, this is it.

The only possible drawbacks are the fact that it plays only two, and I'm not sure about replayability given the limited scenarios out of the box. There's a lot of love for this game and various scenarios out there. Along with an expansion, and I might play this with some regularity if I can find another opponent.

Time to beg the wife to play it.

RATING: 3
Well, the main reason I bought this was to spuport the idea of pre-painted minis. But in that regard it did not impress. There are two sides, and the monster side only has [b]two[/b] different minis!!! One demon, and nine little troglodytes. Boring! Humans are only slightly better. There's one main guy, two semi main guys that LOOK about exactly the same, but actually have different abilities. And then another pair of guys that are about exactly the same. 

The mini situation would be easily overlookable if there was a solid game there. But I have no right to be surprised that it's not that different from similar games that I haven't liked. There's too much randomness from dice. The (somewhat) randomly expanding dungeon is great in theory for replayability, but random in practice, so you're just running around basically aimlessless. 

The most annoying thing is trying to keep track of what a dude on the board is, what his stats are (that can and do change every turn!!!), what his abilities, objects are, etc.

I regret buying this.

RATING: 5
Players represent the demons under New Jerusalem, or the Redeemer forces combating the demons.  Two player battle game where the demons take on the Redeemer player to try and accomplish a scenario's goals.  Simple rules - basically activate, then move and fire, yet full of neat little ideas.  The Redeemer rolls dice and allocates them to their forces, setting their move/combat/defense stats for the turn - it varies.  The demon player rolls three (or four) dice and allocates them to a battle board, which dictates their options for the turn ... recruit, toughen up, tunnel, draw reinforcements or events, etc.  Lovely looking package, huge tiles (almost too big), simple rules, and the game play is fast and a lot of fun.  Both sides play differently, and it does create some nice tactical dilemmas.  Impressive.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Have to give this one a high rating. I was kind of hoping that I wouldn't like it and I could debulk my collection of dungeon crawl games - which always feels baggy comparable to how often they get played - but this is definitely a keeper until I play all the scenarios a few times - which will take ages as there are loads of freely available ones online.

This is an excellent euro-fied dungeon crawl game. With a shortish set up, low rules overhead, quick play time. Generally all good things.

The human player, who I hesitate to call the goodies, use rolled dice to selected rows of abilities, basically combat, defence and movement. Some dice will boast one stat while decreasing another for that turn. As you accumulate wounds you lose the ability to attribute a 3 - say - to a certain character so your options are continually narrowed.

The demon player is playing in a similar way, with an dice allocation board. Some actions you can take need two dice to do, with both even numbers or odd - that sort of thing. This provides quite a few difficult decisions during gameplay and also some really easy ones so turns are quick and the gameplay zips along nicely. If I was introducing the game to someone I would make them the demon player as I think they have the slightly easier roll in terms of rules overhead and additional fiddle. I feel they are also more fun to play as.

There are a few things conspicuously absent from this game that are found in perhaps all the other dungeon crawls that I have played. The most obvious is line of sight rules. In claustrophobia if you on the same tile as an enemy you can attack them. I didn't miss line of sight at all and found it just sped up the game which can only be a good thing.

The game plays only two player and lasts about an hour, maybe slightly more.

I think the tiles though nice are far too large and the tablespace needed for this game ends up being quite large. The models are quite nice - not CMON or GW quality - but come painted which is a nice touch. The price point for this game - when it is freely available - is quite low. The criticism is that for the demon player there is little variation in your units - you have the basic troglodytes and a larger demon whose abilities change depending on scenarios is valid. Though I wasn't fussed by it. This narrowing simplifies the game, but makes all the 'baddies' - with few exceptions - the same. Though, I would love to see this system adapted to another game with a greater variety of models as I think the game system is superb (If you know of one don't hesitate to get in touch!)

I still prefer space hulk to this, but this will get played a lot more while space hulk will gather dust there on the top shelf, bowing the wood under it's colossal bulk.

Addendum: recent replay with SO, this game is ace, it will appeal to euro players, it scratches the dungeon crawl itch, it's not long, it's boss.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
The rating is provisional as we work through the scenarios.

I like this game - the theme, the dice-chucking idiocy of it all, and the ultimate simplicity of the ruleset.  The scenarios can be interesting and it is a great 2p game.

That being said, this will not appeal to puzzlers or eurogamers - this game can't be solved or "mathed".  There is a huge luck factor here and so far it seems that the game is unbalanced in favor of the demon player.  If you have strongly-competitive people playing this, that might be a problem.

On the plus side, the minis are pre-painted!  On the downside, the variety in them is quite small (2 types for the demon player, 3 types for the human player), but that likely accounts for why these can be pre-painted to begin with.  Minor complaint.  It would be nice to have a demon mini for each type of demon (what the demon mini actually is depends on what demon card you have in play for that scenario), but that would drive the price up.

Anyways, one of the things that attracted me to Claustrophobia was that it was 2p, but also that there's a sort of trade-off mechanism that plays - at least on paper - well against itself.  For example, when the humans explore, the demons decide the orientation of the tile.  This is awesome... until you realize that orientation doesn't really factor too much into the game for the most part.  Humans can occupy tiles to prevent demons from spawning.  This is awesome... until you realize the demon player can simply spend dice to break this rule.

Take a step back and the game works.  Its strengths are in the adventure and the embedded story if not its overall design, which isn't to say that it's weak, but more to say that it has its flaws.  The artwork is fantastic, especially the unique tiles (exit, pentacle) and the rulebook is functional - for those of us who are inclined to analyze every rule, however, it is lacking in details and allows for a lot of ambiguity.  Buyer beware.

What I really enjoy about Claustrophobia however is that despite its flaws, it is fun and the two different sides absolutely play differently.  The human player must concentrate on achieving their goals while mitigating risk; exploring can be dangerous and both splitting up and sticking together has its own fair share of danger - it's all a balancing act for the human player (and a lot of luck).  The demon player is just downright a jerk, and needs to be.  Feelings might get hurt here, that's how much of a harassment the demon player must be to succeed.  I like that dynamic.  It is just unfortunate that the game leans towards the jerk instead of the heroes.

Hopefully the expansions, once we get to them, resolve some of the issues, but it's still a fun way to spend a night.

RATING: 7
(As of [b]3[/b] plays) I'm not wild about dungeon crawler board games, as my experiences with [GAMEID=17226] and [GAMEid=59946] have been either too long or too random, respectively. This has quite a lot of randomness, but it is mitigated by clever dice allocation mechanics and is totally acceptable due to the short playing time.

[b]1 year verdict:[/b] Not many 2-player gaming opportunities means this hasn't seen much play, but I wouldn't mind returning to this one. Still one of the only dungeon crawlers to interest me.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
This is a streamlined 2P skirmish game whose greatest selling point IMO is its simplicity. That's either a feature or a flaw depending on what you're looking for. At first it hit the spot, but I must say my tastes gravitate towards heavier fare such as Earth Reborn (one of my all-time faves) and Space Hulk, so I ended up selling the game. Now, learning those games and setting them up is much, much more of an investment than what we have here so I see this as an apple vs orange consideration. 

As far as this game per se, the abstractions make for a simple game as follows. Each tile can hold (in general) up to three figures of each side and each figure can swing at any other figure on that tile. To leave the tile, you must have at least as many figures as the enemy or else your figure is pinned.  Battle is a matter of rolling dice to hit a target on the same tile (there are no "spaces"). 

The de-emphasis on LOS and positioning is made up for -- in theory anyway -- with decisions on how to spend one’s dice and use cards.  The demon player gets to go shopping with the Dice of Destiny each turn for bonuses and has cards to use. The human player has equipment and blessings (bonus powers).  The cards in the game are simple to read and apply. No heavy learning curve here for how to use them or adjudicate which cards take precedence, etc.  

I was initially taken with the game (the pre-painted minis are a nice touch) but quickly grew bored of it. The scenarios felt a bit too samey which I think is not because of how they're written but because of how limited the tactical options for moving and attacking are. Since spacing is not a big consideration, a lot of decisions are just to move guys onto a tile, roll the dice, and hope for the best. I'd rather have specific spaces and have to deal with LOS so as to have a tactical angle in the game. As it is, there aren't a lot of tactical exigencies. 

I think the demon player should be nerfed just a bit by limiting how many cards they can play on one turn, otherwise the strategy is to collect cards until you have some killer combos and then go about wreaking havoc on one monster turn with devastating results. It's a beer and pretzels game with a bit more chrome. Not enough to ultimately hold my attention.

RATING: 6.5
I really like the innovative and unique (at least as far as I know) stat lines for the 'good' guys. Having 6 different stat lines and rolling a die to see what you do that turn is really really interesting and means that you actually have to think when assigning damage to your characters after all if you put the damage in number 3 for example then never again will you get that two movement which might allow you to run away... but if you put it in 6 then your defense is going to be 3-or 4 for the rest of the game thus you will get beaten up more.

Spells and special abilities also have a die number that they trigger on which adds a little to the decision making process.. unless like me you continually roll anything but what triggers your spells :(

Spawning rules for the demon player are very restrictive but the demons can hit quire hard so I suppose this balances out in the end. 

Again I like the die pool for the demon player where you roll 3(plus any bonus dice you my have) and place them either according to the values or whether they are odd or even to trigger certain abilities. 

Really quick for a dungeon crawl game and although the scenarios are heavily in favour of one faction or the other it is quick enough that you can play twice, once as each faction.

The artwork upon the dungeon tiles is superb.

RATING: 10
Impressive how this game can be played INCLUDING SETUP in 30-45 minutes.

In that time I could have set up a Descent quest, chosen characters, equipment, skills, feats, treachery and be completely set for the first turn. But I wouldn't have killed any monsters yet.

Claustrophobia takes the opposite approach and lets players roll dice 3 minutes after the lid comes off the box. And the best thing is, that with games being so short, it doesn't feel as bad when a good/bad luck streak happens.

Update: After several more plays, and even having my GF suggest we play it, I have to raise my rating. This game is the perfect dungeon crawl for me.

RATING: 9
This distills most of the action I want from Descent into a shorter and more tense experience.

Available actions for players on the human side are bound to hit points. Lose a hit point, cancel an action slot. Rolled a die that would let you use that action slot? That character is exhausted (only able to sit and defend his exhausted self). As can be guessed, very little damage needs to be dealt in the game before the tension ramps up and choices start to get difficult. Since the opponent (demon) can never be substantially crippled beyond the span of one turn, time is definitely on the demon player's side.  The only action boundary for the demons is the luck of the dice and how many threat points they've stockpiled during their mini game of demonic Kingsburg.

The combination of these two dynamics makes the game play very quickly and viciously. The decisions, while tense, are often very clear, so down time is minimal unless the demon player starts to get some AP over dice allocation (this goes away with more practice).

A negative: after playing several scenarios repeatedly, I'm starting to see just how much luck is involved in their unfolding. Each team has some ways of mitigating luck, but even some of those methods are themselves greatly affected by the item/action cards that are received at random before the game begins (another layer of luck). It comes down to making the best with what you have, but I can't help but think that some scenarios are sometimes just screwed from the start for one of the players.

I've downgraded my rating to a 9, which is still great on my scale but doesn't meet the "always want to play and this will never change" criterion. It may very well change if someone designs something along these lines with just a little less randomness.

Expansions owned:

[b][thing=100527][/thing]
[thing=162409][/thing][/b]

RATING: 10
Claustrophobia is my highest-rated game:
- The innovative use of dice gives players an acceptable level of control over their own destinies while evening the odds of success between players who have different levels of skill.
- The components are perfect. I love the pre-painted minis because I don't get that nagging feeling that I should be painting instead of playing. It was easy to get my husband interested in playing just by showing him the awesome stuff in the box.
- We can set it up, play it, and put it away in 45 minutes. That's short enough to play during a lunch break or in the evening after work. As a person who owns several epic games and never has time to play them, I love how easy it is to work this one into my day.
- It is designed as a gaming system, with potential over time to have scores of pre-developed scenarios to play and the possibility of developing my own scenarios. I am drooling over the idea of expansions, but the base game contains enough variety to hold my interest for a long time. 
- The designer (CROC) and several experienced players are active on BGG and respond readily to questions. It's incredibly cool to talk to the guy who thought up such an amazing game. 
- It has outstanding tension, excitement, engagement, and immersion. It is fun, Fun, FUN!

RATING: 9
This is an excellent choice if you love fast-playing 2-player tactical minis games. Now that's a crowded field to be sure. But there are some unique aspects that make Claustrophobia well worth looking into. 

First of all, the prepainted minis are an excellent touch and this combined with the quality of the other components really make this a beautiful experience right out of the box. 

Secondly, the dice system is fantastic fun. It provides just enough randomness that you can't get locked into an "I always do this" strategy, but yet provides you with myriad tactical options once the dice are rolled. 

Thirdly, the asymmetric sides feel wonderfully different to play. In many ways, this game is like streamlined Space Hulk. 

I'd give this a very strong recommendation if any of the above is appealing to you. There is very little here not to like.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
A shorter game that manages to capture all the things that make dungeon crawlers awesome in a neat, portable, handy package. It doesn't have character progress within the scenario, but that's made up for with unique mechanics and a very thematic feel.

What I really like is the fast-paced combat system, and generally how quickly a round plays. Over-analyzation is barely possible, but the game presents you with tons of short-term tactical choices nevertheless.

Also a very neat feature is the way the stats are distributed after a dice roll for the human player. This makes play both a bit unpredictable for both players, and deciding which character has which stats for the round a bit of an RPG thing to do.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
In short, Claustrophobia is a dungeon crawler game with high production values and a high depth-to-rule ratio. Where many dungeon crawler games have beautiful minis, boards, cards, etc., Claustro (for short) meets the standard and perhaps brings another level by providing pre-painted minis. However, what Claustro does incredibly well is that it strips away many layers of unnecessary mechanical complexity to get right down to the nitty-gritty while still having an incredibly rich game. Playing within this bare-bones space, Croc (the designer) also creates a rich play space for the demon player. Wherein many 'crawlers the dungeon lord is a malevolent presence (played by the 'good friend' who wants to provide a fun romp for the dungeon-faring folk at their own expense), here, it is both devilish AND fun (e.g., the humans get to pick what corridors they choose to explore [i.e., new tile] but the demon player gets to choose how it is placed, leading to dead ends and closed loops!). By this, I mean that the demon player has rich decisions to make in terms of how it goes about making life difficult for the human player. The asymmetry is also delicious -- while the human player starts off respectively stronger than the demon player, the demon player has the advantage of endurance and tenacity. The little cuts accrew and suddenly the demon player has the upper hand; but it might not be enough to prevent the human player from achieving their goal (to which they should be pretty close to at that point in time!).

Narratively, this asymmetry all comes together in the world of Hell Dorado -- the humans are not the "good guys" but rather complex and flawed creatures who happen to be colonizing hell (to the demons' protest!). Not that the demons are the "good guys" either!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8

While it doesn't have the constant tension of Space Hulk it certainly is a good game that has a quicker play time, very nice pieces and interesting mechanics (human warriors boards to determine stats and how damage is handled and the demon players board that grants special powers based on dice allocation).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.75
An amazing asymmetric two player, dungeon crawl. Quite probably one of the most unique games of its kind. Not only is it a dungeon crawl for two, it plays in 45-60 minutes.

The game has a really cool dice allocation system, where the human player's character's stats can change turn by turn. However as they take damage, different lines are canceled out meaning the humans have to be careful which die they give to each of their heroes. This game is definitely more strategy over "gung-ho-kill-everything-in-sight" and blends great Euro-puzzlyness and Ameritrash mechanics into a nice package.

One side controls the condemned survivors and the other the demon hordes. The base game gives a nice chunk of content and variable scenarios which challenge both sides greatly. However, the expansion, De Profundis, really opens up this game with all the extra content, new characters and scenarios that I highly recommend purchasing with the base game sight unseen. 

However there are a few things that hold this game back from being truly great, one of which is that this game is BIG. The box is an awkwardly long and skinny box, and It will take quite a bit of real estate on a table. I wish the exploration tiles were a tad smaller. Also wish there were more enemy types than what is available currently. It isn't game-breaking at all but it would be welcomed for sure. But the my main beef is that some scenarios aren't fully asymmetric and feel they favor one side over the other. Not a 100% feeling, and one which can be easily mitigated by given the more experienced player the side with the disadvantage. It's something that has been mentioned for a few of the base game's scenarios on BGG which I think were mostly remedied with the expansion, De Profundis. Speaking of which, De Profundis is a must-have expansion to Claustrophobia and I would highly recommend.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Amazing game. Luck and brain burning mixed in an obscure underground adventure. Many scenarios and great story. I enjoy it very much solo as well since both sides play so differently from each other!

RATING: 9.16
[b]2 Player Review:[/b] 

The theme of demons vs the condemned is very strong as you roll your way through the depths of Hell. However, unlike most dice games that have me cursing my luck every time I roll a one, even the ones are of use here. As you assign the dice to either the demons or condemned boards, the strategy is already more prevalent than most combat-heavy games. Of course it does ultimately come down to a dice roll as to whether a hit connects of not, but there are so many ways to increase your chances and position yourself for victory that it makes [i]Claustrophobia[/i] feel more like a puzzle game than anything else. And that`s why I absolutely love it more and more the more I play.

The tile draws can be quite brutal to the condemned as they are often forced back into the pursuing hordes. But it is still a very run dungeon-crawling romp that is over in under an hour. So even if your luck is horrible, the whole adventure is over quickly and you'll only be left with a great story to tell. 

[b]Expansion Review:[/b] 

It's a very welcome addition to the base game. The new tiles, heroes and dogs add a lot more replay value to every scenario. We never play the base game without them. It adds a lot of depth without adds ton of new rules to learn. Two thumbs up!!

[b]Pros:[/b]

- A fast and furious dungeon-crawler that doesn`t outstay it`s welcome after a few bad die rolls.
- The theme is immaculate.
- The game almost feels more like a puzzle with many ways of weighing die rolls in your favor as opposed to more traditional dungeon-crawlers.
- Massive amounts of replay because of the huge number of scenarios and the randomness of the each dungeon layout. 

[b]Cons:[/b]

- Tile draws often hurt the condemned far more than the demons.
- Requires a huge amount of table space.
- Limited demon variety in any one scenario.
- The dogs from the expansion seem a little over-powered after several plays. 

[b]2015 Rating:[/b] 9.15 [b]Rank:[/b] 15 [b]Plays:[/b] 0 - I'm a sad panda. 
[b]2014 Rating:[/b] 9.3 [b]Rank:[/b] - [b]Plays:[/b] 12

RATING: 7
Initial rating one full play 

Judging from some of the comments I think I [i]might[/i] be missing something and that is kind of how I felt through my whole first game, though the point of the game is to just be a simple fast dungeon crawl which it very much succeeds at.  A shame most of the monster figures are all the same.  I really like how the monsters have an order board and even with rolling they have options (maybe more than the good guys, which I played), but overall I just found the game lacked decisions like so many of these types of games do.  

For the good guys it was where to allocate the dice and where to move.  Now we did play the very first scenario, so I am hoping it is really simplified and that some later ones add more the game somehow but lately it seems designers are listening to the many complaints about games being too bloating and going to the other extreme.   Note that games are meant to be played in an hour so only so much can fit in that timeframe much like CR.  Definitely mostly tactical and mostly non-strategic which isn't surprising, luck did not bother me as much as I initially thought it would, its fairly high but it’s a light fast game so not out of place really and it was the lack of decisions that bothered me more. Would like to play a different scenario next time to re-evaluate but overall I think games like Prophecy, Runebound, Castle Ravenloft, Spacehulk etc just aren't really my thing, they leave me wanting more. If you want a good short rules light adventure type game, you can hardly do better than this one.

2017-03-17

I finally played Claustrophobia again :D, it took me awhile but I did it and I enjoyed it a lot. 

I’m unfamiliar with the source material, but I really like its theme. The art is amazing!

I also like that each player plays a very different game, I think I prefer to play as the demon player, but I would play as the condemned as well.

I recently read the rulebook and it has some mistakes, the most important being that the demon player can play the red actions ONCE PER TURN, not per game. Make sure you read the FAQ before you play the game.

Before this last play, I thought I was going to sell the game, but my desire to play the game again is high. I want to explore all the scenarios and I also bought all its expansions. It isn’t the best two player game I have, but, for now, it has a permanent place in my game collection. It plays relatively fast, and you have fun when you play it.  With more plays, the rating could increase or decrease, time will tell, but as it stands, Claustrophobia is very near to become a good game for me.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Claustrophobia upstages the entire FFG catalog, and it's about time.

The premise here is dark: a warrior-priest leads some condemned men on a demon-hunting expedition deep underground. These are desperate, brutal men pitted against hordes of troglodytes. In some scenarios they are trying to escape; in others they have specific objectives, like closing off a portal to hell.

For the humans, the game is always a race against time. They need to explore the surrounding tunnels quickly to find their objective, but if they spread out quickly to cover a lot of ground, they become more vulnerable to attack. At the start of the turn, the human player rolls four dice (one for each character) and allocates them. Each character has six combinations of attack/defense/movement, each pegged to a die-face. This gives the human player some great decisions about battle-formation: who's hunkering down, who's running point, etc. The troglodyte player rolls three dice at the start of the round, and these can be used to obtain "threat points" (used to summon more demons), draw cards, or trigger one-time abilities (making demons faster, stronger, more mobile, etc). The dice-allocation is set up so that the easy baseline is 4 threat points and one card, which is enough to apply continuous pressure. The longer the humans dither, the more troglodytes gather to swarm them, and the more cards can be played to force panics, trigger crazy suicide attacks, etc.

My favorite part of Claustrophobia is the way wounds work for the humans. When a human takes a hit in battle, they must block off one of their die-faces. One or two wounds begin to severely limit their flexibility in battle. It's the best new mechanic I've seen in a fantasy game in years - in a way it reminds me of Magic Realm, which usually puts contemporary fantasy junk to shame.

A breath-takingly produced, fast-paced, tightly constructed game. Highly recommended. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
+ De Profundis
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Interesting, if somewhat baroque, game of exploration and monsters.  A lot of interesting tools in this package for design - swappable demons, the different human items/equipment, etc. - and it's nice to see the range of possibilities in the scenarios published to date.  Extra credit for delivering on the promised web support - many companies say they'll put a lot of scenarios on the web, but few actually come through.  

I think it's more forgiving than Space Hulk, with the typical emphasis of the genre on positioning diverted here to managing the action dice and assorted other limited resources.  Movement and combat are fairly abstract since they are done on a tile basis and are not where the interesting decisions tend to be made.  Because of this, it's easier to play Claustrophobia casually, which will probably help keep it coming back to the table in the future.

Some important errata is out there for this title (changing the invocation of certain demon abilities from 1/game to 1/turn has an enormous impact on play) and you absolutely cannot & do not want to overlook it before playing.  Missing the errata will almost wreck the game for the demon player.

RATING: 7
I've only played one or two other dungeoncrawl-type games, and this one's blown them out of the water. The rules are simple and well-executed; while it's tough on the humans, every scenario seems winnable, and the margins are always tight. 

The real star here is the production values. It's an utterly gorgeous game, it's not horrifically overpriced, it comes with pieces that manage to outshine the ones that come with the deluxe War of the Rings, and not only that, but they have character! The tiles are pretty, the cards are nice...

My only complaint here is that not enough people are buying it to make it a lock for expansions. Seriously, please buy this game. It's money well spent.

[Edit 4/15: Don't enjoy this much anymore - I've played all the scenarios half a dozen times, and for some reason, the thrill is just gone. SAD FACE.]

[BGCOLOR=#339900][COLOR=#FFFFFF]▲[/COLOR][/BGCOLOR] Very streamlined game design: easy to learn, fast to play, rules are so compact that details/exceptions are directly printed on corresponding cards.

[BGCOLOR=#339900][COLOR=#FFFFFF]▲[/COLOR][/BGCOLOR] Well-written rulebook with multiple illustrated examples.

[BGCOLOR=#339900][COLOR=#FFFFFF]▲[/COLOR][/BGCOLOR] Asymmetrical sides.

[BGCOLOR=#339900][COLOR=#FFFFFF]▲[/COLOR][/BGCOLOR] Pre-painted, detailed miniatures.

[BGCOLOR=#339900][COLOR=#FFFFFF]▲[/COLOR][/BGCOLOR] Great artworks (cards, dungeon tiles, cover).

[BGCOLOR=#339900][COLOR=#FFFFFF]▲[/COLOR][/BGCOLOR] Adult, dark and gritty fantasy theme: anti-heroes & demons instead of the usual elves & orcs fare.

[BGCOLOR=#339900][COLOR=#FFFFFF]▲[/COLOR][/BGCOLOR] Great replay value (randomly generated maps, 6 different scenarios).

[BGCOLOR=#FF0000][COLOR=#FFFFFF]▼[/COLOR][/BGCOLOR] Catacomb tiles are arguably too big, requiring players to have a large table.

[BGCOLOR=#FF0000][COLOR=#FFFFFF]▼[/COLOR][/BGCOLOR] Human player's character trays don't fit back in the box once assembled. They can be easily disassembled, but doing so can over time cause damage to the cardboard inserts.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
* Rules:
- The rules are quite simple, which makes the game easier to put on the table after a few months without playing it, which is a big plus.

* Components:
- The rulebook is very clear.
- The art (box, rulebook, material) is very good.
- The miniatures are not as well painted as those of Lord of the Rings: Combat Hex, or not as precisely sculpted as those of Space Hulk 3rd ed., but they are of good quality.
- The tiles are really thick.
- The cards are a little bit prone to damage.  They don't feel too bad, though.
- Idea: I wish that the numerical characteristics had some color code scheme (a shade of red, green, blue, for instance).  This would make them more obvious at a glance.  One probably gets used to the lists, though, but I did not fully succeed after 3 games.

* Game feel:

- The rules are simple and streamlined, which makes getting into the game a real pleasure, as it can be picked and played any time.
- The titles given to the various rule and scenario points really give flavor to the game, and help remember the contents of each point.
- The minis give a really useful and nice visual depiction of the game situation.
- I find myself thinking more about strategy, after a game, than with Space Hulk.  In fact, in Space Hulk, the lessons I get from a defeat are more strategical, and quite simple (like "I should have sent more Genestealers down that hallway").  In Claustrophobia, the lessons are more subtle: "In order to handle the Spadassins, I should have get prepared for the Troglodyte lair tiles, etc.  As for the brute, I should haveâ€¦ etc.".
- The names given to the Demon options and to the cards really give some nice flavor to the game.  They help picture what is going on.
- After ten games, half of them with the demon, its options are quite clear.

** Comparison to Space Hulk
*** Better than Space Hulk
- Painted mini.  They do add a pleasant touch.  They also make the game more attractive to players whom I may want to introduce the game to.  Furthermore, they really draw me more to the game than SH's unpainted pure-red marines.
- Almost no setup time.  SH sees the table less often, because of its longer setup time.
- The scenarios feel more varied, and richer in theme.
- The Demon is more interesting than the Genestealers.
*** Not as good as Space Hulk
- You might sometimes want to put a tile outside of the table space, for strategic reasons (like allowing a character left behind to find a shortcut).
- Figures in Space Hulk die upon a single successful hit: this makes for some great "hurrah" (sp?) moments.  In Claustrophobia, successfully hitting a creature is not as rewarding, as the Humans and Demons take many hits before being killed.  However, this is partially offset by the fact that placing the wound markers requires some interesting choices to be made.
- While the Genestealers plays, the overwatch lets the Marines player roll dice, or take extra actions, if he witnesses a Genestealer movement.  This helps limit the downtime.  The Genestealer player can somewhat study the movements of the Marines while they move: finding the weaknesses in the Marines is important (that's a weaker point).  In any case, there is action, while the Genestealer is waiting, with all the Marines moving.  There is thus less downtime in Space Hulk, for me.  However, maybe this will change: (1) As long as I don't picture all the options of the Demon/Human more clearly, I can spend time thinking about them; (2) When I have a better command of these things, I may use them in order to build strategies (like getting ready in case I get unlucky, etc.).
$ However, after about 4 games, we had learn the options of the Demon and the various cards better, to a point where the game flows clearly better.  As a consequence, I do not get bored anymore, as the Humans.  Plus, I still find it nice to think about whether the Demon player could have chosen better moves.
- Space Hulk feels more "cinematic" and tense to me: SH's narrow passages really make for many griping moments; one has to carefully think about which corridor each Marine should go through, because the guy in first line takes a higher risk, etc.  I guess that the sense of frontal confrontation that you get from SH (with the GS and the Marines basically clashing after a long run in a corridor) is emotionally more gripping than the "pile on them" feeling of Claustrophobia; in SH, it's break or win (?), which is more emotional than Claustrophobia's "let's weaken them a little bit more".
*** Neutral
- The positions of the figures on the board evolve in a more complex way that in Space Hulk, where the squad members tend to remained grouped together, and where strings of Genestealers are likely to form along the narrow passages.  The result is that the "story" told by Claustrophobia is not as clear and powerful as the story in Space Hulk, which is more like a movie in slow motion, where all figures seem to spend the game moving towards simple goals.  However, Claustrophobia's story can thus be more complex and varied.
**  # End of Comparison to Space Hulk

* Miscellaneous:
- Having almost 20 scenarios feels good.  I like having scenarios: they can give a different feel to each session.  The official bidding mechanism is a great addition, for more seasoned players; I love having play-tested rules to guide me, instead of having to devise house rules that may be flawed.
- Having only 3 different human characters, and 2 demon characters is really not an issue for me: Space Hulk works well with even fewer different types!

RATING: 7
When I opened the box for the first time, I was very impressed with the quality of (most) of the game.  The cards are very smooth feeling and easy to shuffle and grab. The dice are a nice mat finish makes then easy to grab out of the Human's Stat "Caddy". 

Only really 2 complaints on the quality of components of the game. I expected the "caddies" to be a little sturdier, but I guess it makes sense since you need to remove the stat cards for easier storage. And the painting on the figures could be a little more distinct (as I've seen several people say here) One of the condemned blades has a black sash in the picture on the card, but both have red on their figures.  The only difference is their hair color. Just something more distinctive would make easier to glance at and know which is which.  

After 1 play, I think this game is very easy to learn.  Reading thru the book, some elements are confusing, but once you are in a game, it all becomes clear. 

Had a blast playing this, and can't wait to go the first scenario a few more times then going on to a new adventure.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Gloriously technocoloured dungeon tiles, cuddly little demons and musclebound hulks wielding giant waffle irons (or hammers, perhaps) ... Claustrophobia certainly hits all the right spots in appealing to my inner ten-year-old. In a pleasant and unexpected turnaround, the game is fresh and clever enough to entice my outer adult, too. Apart from the totally brilliant action/wound system for the human side - one of those ingenious ideas that seems obvious and simple, but only in retrospect - the resource allocation for the depth-dwelling demons is also well done and not just a rehash of what has gone before.

The only criticism I could think of is that the inclusion of the apparently inevitable action/event cards detracts a bit from the outstandingly good core engine of the game. It probably helps regarding variety, however, and since I will play this one more often and possibly even buy it, I might change my mind on this small nitpick, too.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This is a gorgeous box of awesome wrapped around a simple, engaging, enjoyable game. I have no idea how they can sell this for the price point it's at -- I paid something like $50 for it on Amazon, and the components are top-notch and then some.

Reading the rules, I found myself nodding; things worked the way they seemed like they should work. There aren't a lot of rules, and all of the exceptions are pretty much contained to cards and tiles and may or may not arise. Great presentation.

The game itself is a blast. It perfectly models the tension each side is supposed to feel: The humans weaken over time, can't spread out or clump up too much, and need to squeeze out every advantage they can; the demons have endless numbers, but fewer choices on most turns, and the humans can be tricksy.

Based on two games -- same scenario from both sides -- it's both easier and more enjoyable to play the demon. The demon's cards are excellent, and the Destiny board is a great mechanic. The humans have both more and fewer options, and their choices seem to drive the pace of the game. With handicap variants provided, even if the demon=easier problem persists over the course of a few more games, it looks eminently fixable.

One minor niggle with the otherwise stellar components is that the tiles tend to curl a bit, becoming slightly convex. They don't seem too hard to press back flat, though, and it doesn't really impact the game.

This is one hell of a lot of enjoyment for the price, accessible, easy to teach, and tons of fun.

RATING: 8.5
Claustrophobia, to my surprise at least, is a very good game, and quite rich in theme.  As I have stated in my other reviews, theme is very important to me.  From what I initially read about the game I was worried the mechanics were a bit too abstract \ random to capture the theme.

Depending on the dice a player rolled, the player had different abilities and stats to use for that turn.  I found it odd when compared to other skirmish games and tabletop war games.  However, I am happy to say it works.  Dark magic can be fickle, and warriors respond differently to stress \ fear and become less predictable.

The game is easy to learn and play, and doesn't take too long to play.  The missions are varied and fun.  Another feature I enjoy is asymmetrical sides which makes the game more interesting for both players.  Not to mention the components are fantastic, and the miniatures are all pre-painted (not many games have that).

Some say the theme is dark, but to me that is a selling point!  Highly recommended.

RATING: 8
It is rare to see an incredibly thematic game like a dungeon crawl have such tight balance and mechanics as this.  The dice rolling is there, but somehow the game feels liberated from the slavish devotion to the same process of dice-chunking-conflict-resolution that makes other game of the like slow and frustrating.  Decisions in the face of luck, unbelievably tight balance, and controlled play time show the games wonderful eurobased design despite being so crawl-like.  And what is more, is that despite all of this mechanical polish, the game somehow manages to tell wonderful stories centered around the Condemned. Some times the feeling of "I cant believe hat just happened" makes a lost game incandescent as an experience, a rarity for something so mechanically tight. Face it, Claustrophobia is a unicorn.

RATING: 9
Great little game that's easy to learn, teach and play. It has a great theme, simple but effective mechanics and an entertaining mix of skill and luck. The components are top notch, and the rules are relatively clear and well organized.

The limited number of scenarios and monster types is a minor negative, but one that is more than made up for by the quality of game play.

Individual games can be lopsided, but overall game balance seems good. That is, if you played it 10 times, you'd see a relatively equal win distribution and a number of close games between players of similar experience.

I understand there is errata: the red-lettered options can be used once per turn by the baddies, rather than once per game. I actually think it works as well with the "incorrect" rules.

This is a highly recommended game for people looking for a quick, two-player dungeon crawl

RATING: 6
Consider me impressed. I've shunned miniatures games and might continue to do so, but not this one. Rules were straightforward, but you felt like you had a lot of options on your turn. The variability built into the game was impressive: assymetric sides that seem to play very differently, different scenarios, different characters, different boards, different cards. It just seems like every game would feel fresh.

Furthermore, this captured the best parts of dungeon-crawling in a condensed, quick-playing format. As a former D&Der, I've always enjoyed the exploratory aspects of the dungeon delve and the suspense of a fight. However, I'm the first to admit that "old school" D&D (without minatures) was sometimes hard to visualize and its combat frequently boring, but more recent versions seemed far too bogged down in tactical detail, becoming boring in a completely different way. In Claustrophobia, you don't know what's coming around the next corner, combat is quick and to the point, and everything is there right in front of you, in spectacular visual detail. It never bogs down or feels like too much.

The components are superior.

All in all, while I'm not sure this is a genre of game I'll ever love, I definitely found this example of miniatures gaming to be quite solid. Worth exploring more.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.9
It's a classic adversarial dungeon crawl as one player takes the part of the adventurers and the other is the monsters. In the fluff, apparently the gates to hell are opening so naturally the forces of good respond by sending down a few expendable convicts supervised by a religious fanatic of some sort - the sculpt is more than a little reminiscent of a priest of Sigmar from the world of Warhammer.

Anyway, the next twist here in gameplay is that each of the characters have six statlines with differing abilities (move/attack/defence); at the start of each round a die is rolled for each character and is then assigned (player's choice) to each character's stat line.

Wounds are also taken on statlines so that when a character incurs an injury that statline is lost to them so if, say, a guy has taken a wound on line three if his (and they are all he - no female convicts or lady priests in these caverns) assigned die is a three then he is immobilised for the turn.

The warrior priest guy also has a number of abilities that can be activated on certain die rolls. As the game progresses difficult choices have to be made around assigning dice which is a lot of fun.

The player controlling the monsters has activation tokens to spend and the key to their game is controlling how they expend these tokens; knowing when to husband their resources and when to go for the smackdown.

The miniatures that come with the game are quite good and ripe for repainitng (though the off-the-shelf paint job from Asmodee is perfectly serviceable) and the components are of good quality.

So, all-in-all this is a winner. Highly recommended if you're after a tactical dungeon crawl with interesting mechanics. Will consider purchasing.

RATING: N/A
This is a fairly light dungeon crawler. You lead a team of convicts against a pack of demons. This requires a DM.

You roll dice and assign them to the different players. Instead of HPs, you remove the ability of the player to use rolls and they miss their turn.

Sounds kind of interesting. Opposition is somewhat monotonous sounding, though.

RATING: 6
Incredibly atmospheric 2-player game.  Simple to learn, fun while it lasts and the components are outstanding! 

However, it's simplicity is also it's downfall.  There is limited scope to try out new strategies because it's usually quite obvious what step you should take next and the humans become more and more frustrating to play as the game goes on as your actions become limited. I know there are some that like this aspect of the game. 

The different scenarious help to keep the game fresh to some extent.  Ultimately though, due to the lack of variable powers/characters there isn't much to keep you coming back.  The expansions may help remedy this.

RATING: 8
To me it feels like a cross between Euro and Ameritrash style games.  The initiative phase, where you roll dice and then assign them to gain specific abilities, feels like a euro game style mechanic - in that it is somewhat strategic.  The remaining phases (ie movement, attack, events), where you throw dice to determine outcomes are more luck-based and tactical.

The game play perfectly compliments the beautiful components and the game's lush theme. If you’re the humans, you really feel like you’re in a dungeon struggling to survive amongst the hordes of demons. You'll be lucky if you make it out alive! If you’re the demons, it's great fun trying to kill off the humans one-by-one. 

Claustrophobia is a tonne of fun!

RATING: 8.5
This game rocks hard. 

It's a dungeon crawl-esque game that plays in 40-60 minutes. It is for 2 Players but more can play if the hero characters are divided up - but it works best with 2.

What sets it apart is that the evil player has some real decision making to make in this game rather than just spawn, move and attack. This is done by rolling dice each turn and then allocating these to a Threat Board that can grant him powers and special abilities for the turn.

The heroes also have to roll dice each turn and 1D6 is allocated to each hero. Each number used then sets the stats for each hero. The trick here is that if a hero is given a dice value that matches the location of a wound, then they are exhausted and can do nothing but defend (poorly) for the coming round. So careful decision making is required of the hero player(s).

If all this wasn't enough, each scenario uses large tiles and these are randomly drawn, meaning the heroes must explore and never know what is around the next corner. Various tiles also have special rules associated with them, which requires both sides to adapt quickly to the changing landscape.

The game looks fantastic with production values through the roof. Pre-painted minis, gorgeous artwork on the tiles and good components (think Formula D trays) for the heroes.

Claustrophobia is a tense, gritty, edge-of your seat kind of game. It has stripped out most of the fiddly rules of other Dungeon Crawls and left the players with a streamlined rule0set that lets them play and enjoy the experience. This is the best game I have found in a long time.

RATING: 3
This is not a cheaper and better Space Hulk; the little I've played has left me really dumb-founded regarding the lots and lots of praise it got - especially since most its rare detractors on BGG simply only seem to dislike it because they don't like the genre (and more specifically, its dice-driven combat) to begin with.

Sure the peg mechanic and the dice board feel kind of innovative, but I have not seen really interesting decisions related to them so far. The strategy is not found there at all, but rather in the human player to plan around the spawning rules by blocking the rear of their boringly-moving-forward bus with their tankiest character and enough additional damage to clear the threat. For almost every single scenario on almost every turn. No saving grace is found in fights; the problem with tile-driven (no tactical grid) skirmish games (especially with almost 100% melee units) being that their combat system has to get depth somewhere else than positioning - which Claustrophobia simply doesn't care about. It's not the occasional hard-to-play-around event card that will change much.

RATING: 6
Dicey-dungeon crawl.  Love the miniatures and game board graphic designs.  I freakin hate dice though.

Played 2 scenarios.  I feel the good side is slightly favored.  I have no luck with dice, so this may be a coincidence.  The trogs were always easily eliminated.  Allowing only a max of three trogs in a room seems a little too limiting.  5 would be better in my opinion.  It is bad enough that the evil player has to gain tp which takes up a turn to purchase trogs.  It is horrible to see trogs vanish on the account of my opponent's 'good' rolls and whatever insignificant damage I inflict only healed  easily by the redeemer.  Some of the board pieces did allow for some strategic elements, but even they were too constricting.  Narrow passageways, for instance, let the evil player have one trog in the hall along with one good player piece.  The trog is nothing but a speed bump easily run over.  

Some of the cards that you roll for were useless.  The threat portion is so crucial for the evil player.  Giving up a dice for a card is a stretch when it may not amount to anything.  It is worse when you get two of the same card back to back.

Can't hate on it too much...  Theme is really cool.  The bits and the board add to it.  I like the multiple scenarios.  replayability was thought out carefully by the designers.

RATING: 7
規則:
*根據選擇的場景做初始設置
*每輪分成四個階段，進行數輪直到有一方達成勝利條件
1.初始階段 人類玩家擲同等自己操控模型數的骰子，並分配給每個腳色一個放在對應參考表上，對應骰子列為該角色此回合的參數(移動攻擊防禦)，如果該欄有受傷標記，則此角色昏迷不能使用對應該欄的物品卡，且無移動攻擊或天賦，防禦為3，超過角色數的骰多的不使用
*如果當回合治癒了放骰的那欄，則可正常行動
2.人類行動階段  每個腳色可移動跟攻擊，哪個先都可以但不能交錯做，也可都不做
*可使用回合一開始抽的優勢卡
*物品裝備跟者腳色一輩子，不能移除交換，死掉棄掉
3.威脅階段 惡魔玩家擲三顆骰(可能因為上回合能力多擲)，然後分配骰到惡魔圖板，紅色字一回合只能做一次，放完骰後惡魔玩家可放小怪進場，1隻要1點威脅點數，大怪要5點，放置時每個板塊最多三隻，且要有開口(連到邊緣未探索)沒有人類玩家，可出事件卡，無手牌上限
>任意骰點 下次威脅階段多擲一顆
>多顆全部偶或奇數(可多次)  兩個威脅點數
>兩顆奇數骰(可多次)  小怪移動力+1
>一顆奇一顆偶 小怪防+1直到下次威脅階段，只要有一隻在人類行動階段死掉獲得2威脅點數
>兩顆偶數 小怪瘋狂
>一顆3以上(可多次) 抽一張事件卡
>點數和7  怪物可從玩家在的板塊進場，但該板塊還是要有開口
>點數和11 怪物可從無玩家在的任意板塊進場
>點數和9 直到下次威脅階段，所以你的怪可無視移動規則移動，對方英雄失去無視規則移動能力
>12點以上 選擇一個英雄少一滴血，該英雄選擇少哪行
4.惡魔行動階段 同人類只是不能探索板塊
***行動階段規則***
*移動一個板塊一點，探索選擇方向抽1個板塊花一點(人類數目也要跟惡魔一樣)，放置時由惡魔玩家選擇板塊方向但一定要能相連人類選的方向，並打人類移動過去，每個板塊兩邊最多3隻腳色在上面，板塊上有兩方腳色時，數目要一樣多才能移走(阻擋規則)
*如果探索抽的板塊會導致場上完全沒開口，則抽新的取代
*戰鬥時選擇攻擊目標(全部小怪算一個目標)擲等於戰鬥力數目的骰，骰數大於等於目標防禦力造成一點傷害，小怪直接掛，大怪放傷害標記，人類放傷害標記到圖板行動列上
*防禦力最高到6，造成傷害人類如果放到當前行動列並不會導致昏迷
**天賦***
>難以追摸 無視人數的阻擋規則移動
>瘋狂  所有攻擊骰可重擲一次
>保鑣 可代替同格腳色受傷害
>阻擋 阻止腳色離開，跟難以追摸能力會抵消
>祝福 初始階段放置祝福標記選擇面在另外一位角色上，如果骰數剛好對應受傷烈則移除受傷標記，此能力每場景只能用一次
***不平衡調動***
*惡魔玩家移除lost*1 panic*2的事件卡，起始多三點威脅點
*人類玩家多抽一張優勢卡，並未救世主多選一個禮物
**有經驗玩家**
*起始21點往下喊標當人類玩家，之後分配點數拿起始物品，禮物卡2點一張上限4，傭兵3點每隻最多各2，物品卡2點每張，優勢卡1點每張隨機抽

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Ahhh, a dungeon crawl bash-em-up that plays in an hour and has meaningful and agonising choices for both players each turn. There's minimal text driven ability manipulators, so movement and combat are uberfast to execute. The first hard decision each turn is with the human player who must roll 1 dice for each of his warriors (4 or so dependent on scenario) and allocate a result to each warrior. In a cunning process, each warrior has 6 sets of [movement, # of attack dice, defence value], usually offsetting each other, and the die result you allocate to the warrior dictates what set of values it has this turn. Each time a warrior takes a hit, one of those sets disappears from use. Hit all 6 and they're dead, baby, dead. On the demon side the hard decision is again dice based, where the 3 dice you roll can get used in any of a dozen ways - gain Threat Points to bring on bad guys, get event cards, etc. It’s hard because you want everything now. Combat is simply roll however many attack dice you're allowed and hit each time you're >= the target’s defence value making turns quick once the hard decision’s been made. Scenarios seem to be generally based around explore / escape or explore / kill the boss, each with a twist, where success for either player seems to continually hang by a thread. Fast paced turns, the right level of chrome (event cards, etc) to mix things up without slowing things down, easy rules, lovely components. Lots to like if you're looking for a thematic fun ride without having to kill a whole night.

Played a few more times. Even with the different scenarios it gets old if you play it often. But two-player games often do. 

It's obvious that it's designed to be more difficult for the humans, but that's ok as long as you get to switch sides between games :-) It's always fees good to win as human!

The more I play the more I feel that the human player really need a way to vary his actions. The demon player have his cards, the human will only have a few cards each game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A 2 player dungeon crawler with an incredibly dark theme and it has all pre-painted minis. Count me in! While the game is rather light on rules, it makes up for it with the variety of scenarios to keep each game fresh. Both sides play asymmetrically which allows for more replayabilty as it's different depending on the side you're on. The humans have stats depending on the die used and as they take more damage, they have to block those stats. It becomes more and more tense as the game goes on. The demon player has weak creatures, but an unlimited supply.

The game is  favored more towards the demon player, but nothing that a handicap suggestion in the back of the rulebook doesn't fix. The biggest complaint I have of the game is the sprawling nature of the tiles. It's completely unpredictable in how the dungeon unfolds and as the tiles are quite large, halfway through the game, you're needing to shift the map one way or the other to prevent it from running off the table. Overall, it's a solid game that fills in the 2 player dungeon crawl nicely.

Do note that the rules are incorrect about the red text for the demon player. It's once per TURN and not per GAME! That's quite the oversight in the rules.

RATING: 9
This game fills a niche in my heart carved out by Hero Quest.

Similar in feel to Descent, with rooms instead of grids (so, if you're okay with doing away with range, square-by-square movement,  line of sights requirements, etc... you're in for a treat).  Combat is more Final Fantasy and less Chess.

The mood and theme of the game has to do with a group of humans delving into a dungeon inhabited by evil creatures. Tunnels are tight and enemies are dangerous. As the humans explore, they are being worn down. Someone dies, and the rest of the party presses on. The more and more people are hurt, dying, or dead, the bleaker things look for the survivors. If the light at the end of the tunnel is not reached, soon there is no hope left for the sole survivor. 

It's horror zombie movie meets D&D.

This kind of feeling translates beautifully to the mechanics of the die-roll initiative. As humans are injured, you have less and less spaces to place your die roll without the humans being "Exhausted." When a hero dies, that's one less die you get to roll, period. Exhausted heroes are basically punching bags if there are any baddies around. So, it only goes downhill faster. Morale is dropping. People are spending time tending the wounded. The mechanic faithfully recreates the feeling of tension one gets from watching survival horror.
