RATING: 8.5
A great dungeon crawler for two, that won't eat your whole Sunday. Beautifully done and the core mechanics are easy to grasp. Asymmetrical design, makes the human and evil forces game quite different. The tile artwork is gorgeous, the figures itself are ok (not mindblowing, but the paintjob is just ok), the card artwork is just generic fantasy - nothing outstanding, but still within the theme. The dice assignment mechanics are exceptionally well designed and fit the game quite well, realistically - remember all those other games you won while having 1 health? Not here. There's a good chance you'll just faint and be seriously weakened by your wounds, making an easy prey. Preserving all human heroes is crucial. 

Be careful, though. It is what it is. It's a streamlined game that you can finish in 1h. There's no army here, no huge sheets with tons of stats, no 100 kinds of modifiers and items and spells. If you get through this mindset and understand that it was created for a different kind of gameplay, you'll learn to love it. There's a lot of tough choices and each your move can spell your doom. Obviously dice add randomness to this, but as always, it's game of calculating chances and increasing positive dice result. Strike, when it makes sense to strike, hold back, when the odds are against you. But maybe you just want to go berserk and try some wacky lucky attacks. And it may succeed. Which is fun.

See, this game, tells a great story. Whatever scenario you will pick, you can really feel the action. You can even name all those human fellas, and add some backstory while playing the game. Evil player can make squeaky noises, horrible screams or shady laughter. You can immerse in the game, because it doesn't require you to melt your brain in constant calculation and analysis paralysis. It's an action game. After finished session, I always think (and hear) - "gee, I really could have go there, or avoid this".

Be aware that it's not a game that is meant to be always "fair". Some scenarios make it quite hard for humans, which means, it's a bigger challenge. Then again, they are in the heart of hell, and just a bunch of them, so, yeah, what would you expect? Teenage Mutant Ninja Turtles facerolling the place? You should be scared and constantly threatened! And if you win/lose, you can always switch places and see "how it is on the other side". Evil player can choose different methods, from direct attack, to event playing or simple "bite here, bite there" harassment. Those trogs just lurk in the dark and if you won't be careful...

RATING: 7.5
Hands down one of the best mini board games available.

This has over the top production values, especially for the price. Everything inside this box is stunning from the prepainted minis to the thick non warping textured modular board tiles.

This game is also challenging (no matter which side you play) and full of strategy options. Doesn't hurt that it's dripping with theme either!

RATING: 8.6
Excellent game for 2 players, with very simple rules, ideal for newcomers to start in tactical and dungeon games. It´s asymmetric, and with interesting mechanics using dice. In addition, I think this game is awesome, its artistic and production quality is amazingly high for the price (finally, I was able to get it recently, and I am very happy because I had been looking for it for a long time). Miniatures are prepainted and I like them. Many people compare it to "Space Hulk" but, except that both are asymmetric, tactical games for 2 players and both occupy a lot of space on the table, the feeling I´ve when playing "Claustrophobia" is very different. For me, it´s a great game: not better, not worse than "SH". It´s different and lighter. It would be great if it were reprinted by Asmodee, including its expansions. RATING: 8
09-09-2014. I think I like this better than Space Hulk, which I've downrated accordingly.

07-09-2014. Rated after 1 play. Asymmetric 2 player dungeon crawler in which one player plays 'heroes', while the other player plays an overlord-like character. Both sides try to achieve their objectives, which range from escaping, killing or obtaining some other objective.

Mechanisms for actions is innovative. The heroes roll dice and assign it to action-lines on their board that represent the combat, movement and defense values the character will have during the round. The overlord can use dice to activate several of his abilities, gain threat or action cards.

Fun!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
This is the first game in a long time where I just had to shake my head and proclaim ingenuity in the design. It breathes such a fresh air of originality not just into the genre but to board games in general, yet the rules are so simple and elegant.

It's fun allocating dice (and in such different ways for the Humans and Demons), it's fun how the damage system works for Humans, it's fun to build the board up from a single chunky tile, and it's fun how the theme works with little minions flooding the tunnels from unguarded openings.

And I can't rave enough about the components. Before I bought this game, I kept looking for pictures of the minis unpainted (BGG is super misleading with games that come with miniatures; pictures are often tagged incorrectly as "Game" when they should be "Creative") and couldn't find any. Then I looked in the rulebook online, saw the painted minis and laughed that I wasn't going to get hoodwinked by another rulebook that advertised things it provided separately.

And then I opened the box.

All the minis are painted and done very well, with the detail especially evident in the Demon. Strangers would keep stopping by my open box to pick up and admire the figurines, and they would look as surprised as I did when I told them they were pre-painted. At $40 online, and boasting PAINTED MINIS, huge chunky tiles, awesome innovative mechanisms, online designer support, an excellent insert and a satisfyingly huge game box that houses everything securely, Claustrophobia is undoubtedly the best value in board gaming.

5+4

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Probably the best way for me to review Claustrophobia (C) is to compare it to Space Hulk (SH):

1.  Theme:  both SH and C rate highly on this.  I like the world of Claustrophobia, but I wouldn't say the Condemned are as fun to play as Space Marines.
2.  Components.  SH only wins this because I bought the recent 3rd edition set which is phenomenal.  But C components are great, and I love the painted minis.  I just wish you could tell the condemned Blades/Brutes apart from their twins (using something other than hair color).
3.  Map Design/Layout:  slight advantage to SH.  I enjoy the exploration of C, and it does it right - with lots of dead ends and interesting tile types (man, those lairs are rough).  But I prefer having the map of a space hulk laid out before me, and a goal to accomplish.  It really allows for some intense tactical thinking.
4.  Time:  advantage C.  The set-up and play time for a scenario in C is very fast - under 1 hour.  This means my friend and I can play 2-3 scenarios per evening.  A SH scenario (incl set-up) takes much longer.  
5.  Gameplay:  close, but I give the advantage to SH.  I think the mechanics of SH are perfectly meshed with its theme.  Just think Overwatch and having your gun be Jammed; the ranged vs. melee combat of SH provides more high-tension gaming moments.  The one big advantage to C is that the Demon side is much more fun to play than the Genestealers in SH due to the random-die action mechanic.  Very neat, very clever.  You still treat Trogs like cannon fodder, but you have more tactical options to beat down the opponent.

Overall, I give SH an edge in overall rating but Claustrophobia just might see more table time because of its quick setup and play.  You definitely need both in your collection.

RATING: 5
Rating-wise I am a bit torn here. Component (and insert) quality is amazing. With the online senarios, there is an incredible amount of content for the price. I think the game is reasonably well done, and objectively, I think it is probably an 8. 

That said, I just don't find it all that "fun". Mechanically, I think it's cool how damage works, but it does make playing the humans really unenjoyable for me. That is kind of tedious, but due to the luck of the dice, it's not right for the humans to just throw in the towel (or to ask them to do that). So for me, it's more like a 6 or 5.

RATING: 10
Claustrophobia has outstanding components at a great price, but that's just the beginning. It has a ton of play value, too. It's very fast - you can set up, play a game, and have it back in the box again in a single hour. Chances are you'll want to play more than once, though - it's definitely one of those "let's do it again" games. In most scenarios, the human player is exploring tunnels by drawing tiles, and the demon player is trying to kill the humans. It's a slugfest, with lots of tough little decisions to keep it interesting. Switching sides gives you an entirely different experience, because the game is quite asymmetrical.

Not recommended for those who can't deal with random elements, or anyone who is bothered by a theme featuring monsters from Hell. For the rest of you, this is a terrific game - just buy it, you won't be disappointed. My review, which walks you through a solo game step by step, is [url=http://www.boardgamegeek.com/thread/515679/the-dirty-14-dozen]here[/url]. I also wrote a review comparing Claustrophobia to Castle Ravenloft, which can be found [url=http://www.boardgamegeek.com/thread/567476/comparison-to-claustrophobia]here[/url].

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Comparisons to Space Hulk are inevitable, but I prefer Claustrophobia for several reasons.

It's much less atmospheric, in part because Space Hulk's mechanics are, comparatively, very true to its theme: it tries, if you like, to be a simulation. (The timer is particularly vicious -- you can't take five minutes from your frantic life-or-death struggle to consider the options.) The comparative lack of atmosphere is just because Claustrophobia is more gamey.

Where the Genestealer player in Space Hulk has less interesting decisions to make, the demon player in Claustrophobia actually has more choices than the human does. The game's biggest flaw is actually that it's so much more fun to be the bad guys because the choices are so much more interesting. (Its second biggest flaw is that two of the base game scenarios are unplayably biased.)

There is a fair amount of dice rolling, but it's mitigated to some extent by a set of clever dice allocation mechanisms. Random drawing of cards and rooms provides major replayability. 

It does all feel a bit samey after a while, though; I'll never love it enough to want to play it al the time. But I keep it because it feels a hole in my collection. 

The best thing about it is that it can play fast. I can't imagine pulling Space Hulk out on a whim; it just takes too much time and too much energy. Claustrophobia isn't quite as deep an experience, but it's a perfect go-to dungeon crawl.

RATING: 7.5
I really love the art/components in this game and the fact that it plays pretty quickly.  The scenarios are interesting and I like that the rules are streamlined. 

We finished all of the base game scenarios so it is time to try our De Profundis.

As noted in the expansion section we ended up selling this game as my daughter lost interest.

I have always played the human side (my daughter liked playing the Demon side) and I was not a fan of the dice dictating your actions.  I have had several occasion where one of my characters had half their live left but because I didn't roll enough different numbers they had no actions and were quickly devoured.  I much prefer an action point allowance system.

RATING: 8.5
Great fast paced dungeon crawler! 

As human player, you roll and allocate stats and take your turn. The mechanism to simulate the wounding of your men is very nicely done.

As demon player, you roll dice that give you abilities to either spawn or modify your existing creatures, draw event cards or metagame. 

These elegant mechanisms, coupled with really nice art, pre-painted miniatures, scenario variations and equipment, event and advantage cards make for a fast-paced dungeon crawler with lots of variation and an engaging gameplay.

This will probably obsolete both Doom as Gears of War for me.

RATING: 8
This is one of a kind, a dungeon crawler thats not entirely luck based, plays two players, has next to no set up time, isn't fiddly and plays in 45 minutes.  This is an amazing feat with there being so many slow bit driven slogs of games in this genre.  The minis are great and the box design works well.  The over all components are very good quality.  Gameplay wise, it's a pleasure to play, it's fairly light, but that actually helps it shine.  Theres some tension to be had and tough choices around each corner.  While dice driven the asymmetrical mechanics on both sides are extremely strategic and well done, that says something, I wouldn't call this a dicefest even though it uses dice. It's over all highly tactical with some really interesting spawn/line of sight mechanics that make for some very cool choices.  My only beef is that there's not enough variety of demons/heroes in the main box, but, that leaves for what I hope will be many expansions to come.  Still the scenarios are all very similar and there, in the base game is a distinct lack of variety.  But if you want a nice quick dungeon crawl that's an easy teach but interesting play for 2, this is ideal to have in your collection, it fills a spot no other game will in that regard.  I hope we see more from this title in the future.

RATING: 7
My review from the game in finnish: http://www.lautapeliopas.fi/peliarvostelut/claustrophobia/
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
Dice allocation mechanic creates interesting decisions for both sides. The game is close and exciting until the end.

Although there is luck involved in tile draws and combat, I never felt that the outcome of the game was determined by luck.

=Not for you if = 

You don't like sways in your game. Some tile draws (like a dead end) can sway the flow of the game from one side to the other. I think it creates more excitement and balances the game, however, some people might find it frustrating.  

You are looking for a completely balanced game. Some scenarios are not well-balanced, and a few of them are broken. Especially the scenarios with a predetermined layout takes away an exciting mechanic of the game (tile drawing and placement), and they are more likely to be the ones that are not well-balanced. Several of them are good, and can be replayed.


=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Claustrophobia is simple, short, tense and balanced, excelling in these tricky areas where most dungeon-crawl games falter. Components are very much a mixed bag. The tiles are sturdy and nicely illustrated and the painted miniatures are OK but lacking in variety. The various markers are nothing special but are serviceable. The theme really could have been far more appealing as generic humans versus monsters, and I find the whole Hell Dorado mythos detracts as a backdrop - it is unfamiliar and opaque to most of us and I find players just ignore rather than embrace it. A worse decision, however, is having two pairs of human characters use identical sculpts and be differentiated only by one member in each pair having blonde hair. Truly is a bad decision for the ages. The game itself is good enough that it overcomes its absurd theme and other poor choices on the part of the publisher. Again, a dungeon-crawl game with relatively few rules, a short play time and tense, balanced action is a rare bird, and Claustrophobia gets high marks in all those areas.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Extremely fun, quick and easy dungeon crawler.  It's the right kind of dice-chucker.  And the tiles and pre-painted minis are top notch.  It could use a lot more variation on the demon side.  Turns and decisions can be pretty samey from turn to turn.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
Strikingly good dungeon crawl game which is heavy on theme and that shines due to its ingenious use of dice. Human players roll dice and assign one of them to each of their active players. Each number on the character sheet has different figures in terms of movement, combat and defense value of the character. Whenever you receice damage, the human player has to choose one of these lines to be blocked. So later in the game you will have hardly no choice concerning what row to occupy. Sometimes at least one character being stunned is just inevitable. Awesome, next time I want to try our gameplay with the demons. 

A minor criticism: Production value is already way beyond awesome in this game, but when you have two warriors of the same type - why not make them distinguishable. They look the same, they have the same base ---> ok, I was now pointed to the fact that the guys have different hair-colour. So after all you can distinguish it. It wouldn't have hurt to make the difference a little more obvious.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
UPDATE #2:  Get it.  The best game I have played so far in 2010.  Tight, thrilling, quick, and immersive.  Don't miss the train simply because one high profile passenger said the ride is a little bumpy.  The scenery is scarily beautiful.

-----

Realize that my comments are following on the heels of two initial plays.  As always, my thoughts and rating on the game could go up or down.  Let me elaborate why I think it will be up....

First off, right now, I like it better than Space Hulk.  SH can be such a beast to set up (I know, that is a terrible excuse), and it has to be handled with kit gloves (man, is it expensive).  But I really feel that Claustrophobia has it beat in more than just those two areas.  Claustrophobia has a ridiculous potential for some very good and very interesting expansions.  And it also seems to have a much better flow.  

Space Hulk is a much more tense game--and it is surprising to me that, for whatever reason, I am OK with a lesser level of tension in Claustrophobia.  The tension in Space Hulk is unparalleled--it stands head and shoulders above any other game in that area.

But the choices that are present in Claustrophobia, small as they might appear, are what really make the game work for me.  Make no mistake--they are the clear and present Euro element in this otherwise purely American game.  And it cannot be stated that these choices make the game run, in the way that the choices in a pure Euro do (say, Goa or Agricola).  However, these choices exist to give the player a certain feeling of control over what happens in the game--even if that feeling is just that--a feeling.  Far from arbitrary, and far from dominating, these choices are what make the game stick together, even in instances when pure chaos threatens to blow the holy doors off the whole thing, and send it crashing into the ranks of the ridiculous.  One game, the game was down to the wire, and I won merely because I had to roll a one--and I did.  

I love Claustrophobia.  Yeah, I think the theme is stupid, almost childish in its attempt to gain credibility with the Warhammer and FF crowd.  Seriously, why demons?  Nevertheless, the game does not seem to be so evil and devious as to be avoided.  And I like it better than Space Hulk.  For now.

UPDATE:  After a third play, I have thought of some more reasons why I like this game so much.  Because there are no hexes/squares--you are simply on a large tile--there are zero line-of-sight issues.  Add this to the fact that with one minor exception, all combat is done hand-to-hand, and you are left with a streamlined design where battle is vicious, quick, and ever-present--with no LOS questions, no range questions.  Nothing but battle, which leaves players to simply play the game and weigh the aforementioned choices.

RATING: 6.5
I was really excited when this game was released, but after one play I have no desire to purchase it. It is quite a good game, it is just that it is too random to be a gamers' game and too elaborate to be a family game. So, depending on my mood, I am afraid that I would always choose either Space Hulk or HeroScape over this game.
Still it has quality components, great artwork, a nice tile system and some interesting movement rules. It really is too bad that the dice rolls, cards, abilities and tile properties hardly let you plan ahead. The designer should have replaced the character dice rolls with fixed statistics and command points. And the wound markers with markers that can be assigned to different body parts (to lower the statistics of your choice when you get hit). I really do not like it that the models have 2 movement points during one turn, and zero during the next (because I rolled badly). And that the monster player may receive actions cards each turn that make exceptions to the rules and contain quite a bit of text. Also, the translation of cards and rulebook from French is mediocre at best.

RATING: 9
UPDATE: Rebought in July 2014 and rating upped from 3.5 to 9. I'm not expecting Descent: First Edition but shorter, which was what I wanted/expected when I got it first time around. I'm also more open to competitive games than when I owned it last. As such, it's a nice light dungeon crawl that competes in the slot of the D&D Adventure Games (coop). It's not a tactical combat game - in fact, it's more like a cross between Kingsburg and a dungeon crawl. It's a dice placement game with a dungeon crawl attached. Taken as what it is, and not what I wanted it to be a few years ago, I like this one.

UPDATE: Very, very boring... Claustrophobia is beautiful, but a limited range of monsters and special actions make it a bit of a snoozeathon for the demon player. Jon, who plays the good guys, didn't find it especially exciting either. All in all, a bit meh.

A light combat/dungeon crawl game with beautiful tiles. It feels lighter than the D&D series of cooperative games. There's less variety of monster, and the demon player's options for actions are controlled by dice rolls and a board.

There's not much room for tactics either. The aim of the game for the demon player is to throw monsters at the opponent until they die or get out. The non-demon player has a small number of different units and needs to get out.

Good for a light combat game taking under an hour. Simple to set up too.

RATING: 4
This is a really mixed bag. It has some pros - the tiles look great, the core rules are streamlined, elegant and easy to understand. I really like the dice allocation mechanism, it's very unique for this type of game.

Unfortunately, Claustrophobia just falls flat to me. Playing as an overlord is pretty cool due to a varied action board, but playing as heroes is simply boring - you don't really have that many choices to make. I wish the heroes had more cards with special abilities in play, this would really spice up the game. It's a shame that one side of the conflict clearly has more fun than the other. 

Another downside of the base game is the lack of variety of the monsters, you only get one type of minions and one "level boss" (yes, the cards can modify their abilities, but the miniatures remain the same, which can get boring).

I gotta say that after all the hype I heard about this game I was really disappointed.

That means each time I play it is like playing it for the very first time and I have to relearn the rules and strategy. Worse, I think I've only ever played the first scenario.

RATING: 6
The movement pinning rules (characters can't leave a room if there are more monsters than good guys) do an admirable job of promoting group interdependence and cohesion.  There are other things to like, too: tile exploration, dice assignments that affect character traits, turn-to-turn variable overlord powers, etc.

Since it's a two-player game, it won't be played often - but that's just fine for the sake of replayability and freshness.

[i]Update:[/i]

Rating lowered after playing through the six-scenario "campaign".  Probably deserves a 5 rating, but I saw a rainbow today and am in a good mood.

The game's repetitive and samey, and lopsided in favor of an evil player who loves events and spawning tricks.  The tentacle rooms are the worst.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.8
I’ve read a lot lately about this game. In almost every article, review or video about this game, everybody mentions the high quality of components. Well, to be short on this. They are right. Even the dice are high quality dice. And the pre-painted miniatures are just fantastic. Another thing that I read everywhere is how tactical this game is. Again, everybody is right. The Formula-D style boards for the hero player are very nice, and when a die is disabled for a hero, that really is a handicap for that player. The way the monsterboard works, is very nice. Also the balance between good and evil is very good. I don’t have the feeling that there is a big advantage for 1 or the other party. But….

All of the great aspects of the gameplay in the game, is destroyed (well, that is a very big word, but I don’t know a lighter one for it), by the luck that comes with the dice. Everything in this game is controlled by dice. If the hero player has bad luck, and he throws 4x a 4, and all 4′s are blocked, all he can do is. Nothing. This happened at our 1st play of this game. M. suffered from a lot of bad luck. She didn’t manage to throw a 3 or higher when she attacked me, while I had all the luck in the world. If I needed a 5 or higher, I threw a 5 or higher to hit the hero. Also M. suffered from bad luck with drawing the cards. While all the event-cards I draw, where very useful. To be short on this one, it was a flawless victory for the monsters.

At this moment, we have mixed feelings about this game. Perhaps we have to re-read the rules, but I’m pretty sure, we didn’t do anything wrong according to the Dutch rules (of course it’s possible, that it’s not a great translation, so I’ll read the English rules). We enjoyed playing, even while the theme is not our ‘thing’, in basic the mechanics are very nice, but at our play, they were ruined by bad / good luck. Maybe we have more leveled luck with our next game. It sure tastes like more.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
